	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">2020 coronavirus pandemic in Pakistan</h1>

	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Details of ongoing viral pandemic in Pakistan</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>

<p>The <a href="/wiki/2019%E2%80%9320_coronavirus_pandemic" title="2019–20 coronavirus pandemic">2019–20 coronavirus pandemic</a> was confirmed to have reached <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> in February 2020. As of 30&#160;March&#160;2020,<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2020_coronavirus_pandemic_in_Pakistan&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> the number of confirmed cases in the country is 2039, with 82 recoveries and 26 deaths. <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_Pakistan" title="Punjab, Pakistan">Punjab</a> is currently the region with highest number of cases at over 700.<sup id="cite_ref-govt_tracker_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govt_tracker-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Multiple regions across the country have imposed lockdowns until early April to stem the outbreak. These include Punjab,<sup id="cite_ref-punjab_lockdown_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-punjab_lockdown-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Sindh,<sup id="cite_ref-sindh_lockdown_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sindh_lockdown-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Balochistan<sup id="cite_ref-balochistan_lockdown_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-balochistan_lockdown-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> and Azad Kashmir<sup id="cite_ref-ajk_lockdown_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ajk_lockdown-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> while Gilgit-Baltistan has imposed lockdown indefinitely.<sup id="cite_ref-gb_lockdown_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gb_lockdown-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2020_coronavirus_pandemic_in_Pakistan" title="Timeline of the 2020 coronavirus pandemic in Pakistan">Timeline of the 2020 coronavirus pandemic in Pakistan</a></div>
<p><br />
</p>
<div class="barbox tright" style="overflow-x: auto;">
<div style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:740px; background: white;">
<table style="text-align:left; border-collapse:collapse; width:100%;">
<tbody><tr style="background:none"><th style="text-align:center;" colspan="5">COVID-19 cases in Pakistan<span class="nowrap">&#160;&#160;</span>(<div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:2019%E2%80%9320_coronavirus_pandemic_data/Pakistan_medical_cases_chart" title="Template:2019–20 coronavirus pandemic data/Pakistan medical cases chart"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:2019%E2%80%9320_coronavirus_pandemic_data/Pakistan_medical_cases_chart" title="Template talk:2019–20 coronavirus pandemic data/Pakistan medical cases chart"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:2019%E2%80%9320_coronavirus_pandemic_data/Pakistan_medical_cases_chart&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div>)<br /><span style="margin:0px; font-size:90%;"><span style="border:none; background-color:Black; color:Black;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;Deaths</span><span class="nowrap">&#160;&#160;&#160;</span><span style="margin:0px; font-size:90%;"><span style="border:none; background-color:SkyBlue; color:SkyBlue;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;Recoveries</span><span class="nowrap">&#160;&#160;&#160;</span><span style="margin:0px; font-size:90%;"><span style="border:none; background-color:Tomato; color:Tomato;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;Active cases</span>
<div class="nomobile" style="text-align:center">
<p><span class="mw-collapsible mw-customtoggle-feb mw-customtoggle-feb-l15" id="mw-customcollapsible-feb" style="padding:0 8px">Feb</span>
<span class="mw-collapsible mw-customtoggle-feb mw-customtoggle-feb-l15 mw-collapsed" id="mw-customcollapsible-feb" style="border:2px solid lightblue; padding:0 8px">Feb</span>
<span class="mw-collapsible mw-customtoggle-mar mw-customtoggle-mar-l15" id="mw-customcollapsible-mar" style="padding:0 8px">Mar</span>

</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="February_2020">February 2020</span></h3>
<p>On 26 February, Pakistan confirmed its first two cases of the coronavirus. <a href="/wiki/Zafar_Mirza" title="Zafar Mirza">Zafar Mirza</a>, the Prime Minister's Special Assistant on Health, stated in a <a href="/wiki/Twitter" title="Twitter">tweet</a>: "I can confirm first two cases of coronavirus in Pakistan. Both cases are being taken care of according to clinical standard protocols &amp; both of them are stable."<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The first patient was a student at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Karachi" title="University of Karachi">University of Karachi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sindh_province" class="mw-redirect" title="Sindh province">Sindh province</a> while the second patient was from the federal territory of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Both patients had recently returned from <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Within a week of the first two cases, Pakistan confirmed three more cases, including a case in Pakistan's capital, <a href="/wiki/Islamabad" title="Islamabad">Islamabad</a> and also in <a href="/wiki/Rawalpindi" title="Rawalpindi">Rawalpindi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_Pakistan" title="Punjab, Pakistan">Punjab</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="March_2020">March 2020</span></h3>
<h4><span id="March_1.E2.80.9310_.E2.80.93_Early_spread"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="March_1–10_–_Early_spread">March 1–10 – Early spread</span></h4>
<p>The fifth case was also reported, on 2 March, from the federal area of the country,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> of a 45-year-old woman from <a href="/wiki/Gilgit-Baltistan" title="Gilgit-Baltistan">Gilgit-Baltistan</a>, who had also travelled from Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 6 March, <a href="/wiki/Murtaza_Wahab" title="Murtaza Wahab">Murtaza Wahab</a> announced that the first patient in Karachi had fully recovered and was later discharged from hospital after testing negative.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> On 8 March, Pakistan confirmed its seventh case of COVID-19, also in Karachi.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The next day, Pakistan reported nine new cases in Karachi, meaning that there was a total of 16 cases of COVID-19, with Sindh having the highest number of cases, 13 altogether.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Five of the new patients had travelled to <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a> and some others patients had returned from <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>. Three new cases were confirmed on 10 March, including one in <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad,_Sindh" title="Hyderabad, Sindh">Hyderabad</a> and the first case in <a href="/wiki/Quetta" title="Quetta">Quetta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Balochistan" title="Balochistan">Balochistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="March_11.E2.80.9319_.E2.80.93_Outbreak"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="March_11–19_–_Outbreak">March 11–19 – Outbreak</span></h4>
<p>On 11 March, 76 suspected cases were reported in several districts of Punjab province, including <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">Lahore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gujranwala" title="Gujranwala">Gujranwala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sargodha" title="Sargodha">Sargodha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hafizabad" title="Hafizabad">Hafizabad</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lodhran" title="Lodhran">Lodhran</a>. The Healthcare Department officials informed that ten patients were immediately cleared of the suspicion, while 55 patients were cleared after testing negative.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> A second case in <a href="/wiki/Gilgit-Baltistan" title="Gilgit-Baltistan">Gilgit-Baltistan</a> was confirmed the same day in <a href="/wiki/Skardu" title="Skardu">Skardu</a> leaving the tally at 20.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> A third case was confirmed in Gilgit-Baltistan in <a href="/wiki/Shigar_District" title="Shigar District">Shigar district</a> on 12 March, who had a travel history of Iran and was reported to be under treatment at the Skardu hospital.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> The same day, <a href="/wiki/Murtaza_Wahab" title="Murtaza Wahab">Murtaza Wahab</a> informed that the second patient of the virus had completely recovered.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On 13 March, the Sindh Health Department identified a 52-year-old patient as positive, which marked the first case of local disease transmission as the patient had travelled from <a href="/wiki/Islamabad" title="Islamabad">Islamabad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> 24 of the 27 suspected cases in <a href="/wiki/Khyber_Pakhtunkhwa" title="Khyber Pakhtunkhwa">Khyber Pakhtunkwa</a> were also cleared that day.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> At the end of the day, the total number of cases had risen to 28, with six new cases in <a href="/wiki/Taftan,_Balochistan" title="Taftan, Balochistan">Taftan</a> and another in Sindh.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> By 14 March, the number of cases was 31 as two new patients were found positive in Karachi while one was reported in Islamabad.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Five more cases were announced in Karachi the next day on 15 March, including a second local transmission of the coronavirus in Sindh, while the other three had a travel history of <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> and one had been to Balochistan.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> There was also a new case reported in <a href="/wiki/Islamabad_Capital_Territory" title="Islamabad Capital Territory">Islamabad Capital Territory</a>. Lahore Health Secretary, Mohammad Usman confirmed the first case of coronavirus in <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_Pakistan" title="Punjab, Pakistan">Punjab</a> in the city of <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">Lahore</a>. The infected patient had returned from <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a> on 10 March and was shifted to Mayo Hospital in an isolation ward.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Health_(Pakistan)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Institute of Health (Pakistan)">National Institute of Health</a> reported 11 new cases in Sindh and 6 new in a mobile lab at the Taftan border area. and the first case in <a href="/wiki/Punjab,_Pakistan" title="Punjab, Pakistan">Punjab</a>, increasing the tally to 53.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> On 16 March, a total of 134 new positives cases were registered, the majority of them, 116 in Sindh. Khyber Pakhtunkhwa also reported its first 15 cases<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> while 3 were found in Balochistan. This marked the sharpest increase so far as not only were more than a 100 cases were reported in a province within a day but also the number across the country reached 187.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> The tally had shot up to 237 with 25 new cases in Punjab, 12 in Sindh and 4 in Islamabad on 17 March.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Daily21_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Daily21-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 18 March, the first case of coronavirus was reported from <a href="/wiki/Azad_Kashmir" title="Azad Kashmir">Azad Kashmir</a>. The provinces of Sindh and Gilgit-Baltistan saw an increase of cases by 36 and 10 respectively. New cases were also reported in other provinces. A patient from <a href="/wiki/Hyderabad" title="Hyderabad">Hyderabad</a> was also discharged after recovering in Sindh province, making the total number of recovered cases 5. A total of 302 positive cases were confirmed in Pakistan on 18 March.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The first two deaths due to the virus in the country were also confirmed on the day. Both were reported from the province of <a href="/wiki/Khyber_Pakhtunkhwa" title="Khyber Pakhtunkhwa">Khyber Pakhtunkhwa</a>, the first being a 50-year-old man who had recently from <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mardan_District" title="Mardan District">Mardan District</a> after performing <a href="/wiki/Umrah" title="Umrah">Umrah</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mecca" title="Mecca">Mecca</a>, while the second victim was a 36-year-old from <a href="/wiki/Hangu_District,_Pakistan" title="Hangu District, Pakistan">Hangu District</a>. Both had been hospitalised in <a href="/wiki/Peshawar" title="Peshawar">Peshawar</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The cases doubled by more than half from 33 to 80 in Punjab; and from 23 to 81 in Balochistan on 19 March. The rise in cases led the provincial government of Balochistan to declare a health emergency and impose a ban on public transport. The provincial government spokesperson Liaquat Shahwani stated that a relief package will be provided to the employees of transport companies.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> With a total of 159 new cases, the number confirmed cases jumped to 461.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="March_20.E2.80.9331_.E2.80.93_First_deaths"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="March_20–31_–_First_deaths">March 20–31 – First deaths</span></h4>
<p>On 20 March, the first death was reported in Sindh. The patient was a 77-year-old who had acquired the virus through local transmission.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The patient was a cancer survivor and had other underlying medical problems such as <a href="/wiki/Hypertension" title="Hypertension">hypertension</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diabetes" title="Diabetes">diabetes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> While in other provinces, the increase in number of new cases was lower compared to the past few days at 34 and the tally stood at 495.<sup id="cite_ref-MoNHSRC_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoNHSRC-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 March, the third death in Khyber Pakhtunkhwa was announced. The first death in Gilgit-Baltistan and Balochistan were also announced on that day, meaning that the number of deaths increased to 6. The number of cases had also increased to 784 with 138 new cases.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The fatality at <a href="/wiki/DHQ_Hospital_Gilgit" title="DHQ Hospital Gilgit">DHQ Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gilgit" title="Gilgit">Gilgit</a> was a doctor who contracted the virus after screening pilgrims returning from Iran.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On 22 March, Gilgit-Baltistan went under lockdown for an indefinite period.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> 13 new pilgrims from <a href="/wiki/Taftan,_Balochistan" title="Taftan, Balochistan">Taftan</a> via <a href="/wiki/Dera_Ghazi_Khan" title="Dera Ghazi Khan">Dera Ghazi Khan</a> were put in <a href="/wiki/Quarantine" title="Quarantine">quarantine</a> at <a href="/wiki/Mirpur,_Pakistan" title="Mirpur, Pakistan">Mirpur</a>. Also on that day, <a href="/wiki/Descon" title="Descon">DESCON</a> donated 10,000 <a href="/wiki/Hand_sanitizer" title="Hand sanitizer">hand sanitisers</a> to hospitals in Punjab, whereas in Balochistan 26 drivers who transported the positive COVID-19 cases to hospitals were kept in quarantine.<sup id="cite_ref-MoNHSRC2_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoNHSRC2-58">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 March, many doctors across the nation complained about the lack of proper equipment for battling the virus. A spokesman for Doctors' Union in Khyber Pakhtunkhwa said, "We do not have <a href="/wiki/Personal_protective_equipment" title="Personal protective equipment">personal protective equipment</a> (PPE), or <a href="/wiki/Goggles" title="Goggles">goggles</a>, and even <a href="/wiki/Surgical_mask" title="Surgical mask">[face] masks</a> we are buying from our own funds".<sup id="cite_ref-doctors_complain_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doctors_complain-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Arrangements were made on the day by the <a href="/wiki/Foreign_Office_of_Pakistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Foreign Office of Pakistan">Foreign Office</a> to bring 72 Pakistanis stranded at the <a href="/wiki/Doha_International_Airport" title="Doha International Airport">Doha International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatar" title="Qatar">Qatar</a> as it had decided to temporarily ban travelers from Pakistan and 14 other countries early in the month. The passengers were subject to strict screening upon arrival.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Another flight was arranged to bring 150 citizens for the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">UAE</a> stranded at <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Abu_Dhabi_International_Airport" title="Abu Dhabi International Airport">Abu Dhabi International Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The Sindh Education Minister <a href="/wiki/Saeed_Ghani" title="Saeed Ghani">Saeed Ghani</a> tested positive for the virus and self-quarrantined for 14 days that day.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> He recovered from the virus on 30 March.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 March, Sindh and Balochistan observed lockdown until 7 April, while Azad Kahmsir went under it until 13 April respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-sindh_lockdown_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sindh_lockdown-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-balochistan_lockdown_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-balochistan_lockdown-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ajk_lockdown_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ajk_lockdown-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Punjab also imposed lockdown on 24 March, but only until 6 April.<sup id="cite_ref-punjab_lockdown_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-punjab_lockdown-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In Sindh, the local police detained 472 people in various districts of the province the same day in violation of the lockdown, with 222 of them in Karachi alone and a total of 72 FIRs were registered on 24 March. The cases pertained to hoarding and profiteering of safety masks and hand sanitisers, large gatherings, opening shops and restaurants and travelling in passenger buses.<sup id="cite_ref-lockdown_arrests_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lockdown_arrests-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The provincial government of Sindh allowed 640 pilgrims quarantined in Sukkur to return home after being tested negative for the virus. The Chief Minister issued directives for the relevant deputy commissioners to receive the pilgrims on their return and monitor their health conditions for the next 10 days.<sup id="cite_ref-pilgrims_return_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pilgrims_return-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 March, several restrictions were imposed in the capital territory of Islamabad. These included closing of the outpatient departments of hospitals, complete bans on intra-city, inter-district and inter-province public transport as well as gatherings in public and private places.<sup id="cite_ref-islamabad_measures_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-islamabad_measures-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Three new recoveries were announced as well as the eighth death in the country. The number of positive cases in the nation crossed 1,000 as the tally increased to 1,057.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> On 26 March, 140 new cases were tested positive across Pakistan. One new death was reported in Punjab, meaning that the death toll increased to 9. The total number of cases reached 1,197. Meanwhile, the number of recoveries increased by 2.<sup id="cite_ref-MoNHSRC4_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoNHSRC4-68">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 March, Pakistan reported a record number for new cases detected in a single day with 211. Punjab also overtook Sindh as the province with highest number of cases at 490, while two deaths were also reported there.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/National_Institute_of_Health,_Islamabad" title="National Institute of Health, Islamabad">National Institute of Health</a> (NIH) distributed <a href="/wiki/N95_mask" title="N95 mask">N95 masks</a> across Sindh, while in Khyber Pakhtunkhwa, screeing teams were deputed at all district entry and exit points for screening of visitors of Covid-19 patients. In Gilgit-Baltistan, the local government decided that all travellers coming from the Taftan border would be tested for COVID-19. The total number of positive cases in the country reach 1408, while 3 patients were discharged, making the recovered cases a total of 26 and two deaths occurred, taking the total number of deaths to 11.<sup id="cite_ref-MoNHSRC5_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoNHSRC5-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The NIH initiated district level trainings of <a href="/wiki/High-dependency_unit" title="High-dependency unit">high-dependency unit</a>, isolation and quarantine staff across Punjab.<sup id="cite_ref-MoNHSRC7_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoNHSRC7-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 28 March, the Foundation set up by the Chinese billionaire <a href="/wiki/Jack_Ma" title="Jack Ma">Jack Ma</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Alibaba_Group" title="Alibaba Group">Alibaba Group</a> sent a second aircraft carrying various medical supplies to Pakistan. The aircraft was received in Karachi with at least 50,000 testing kits, large number of face masks, ventilators and <a href="/wiki/Personal_protective_equipment" title="Personal protective equipment">personal protective equipment</a> (PPE), which were combined around two tonnes of supplies worth Rs67 million.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The same day, Pakistan allowed <a href="/wiki/Thai_Airways" title="Thai Airways">Thai Airways</a> to resume its flight operation for Islamabad to bring back 175 Pakistanis stranded in <a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, the Government of Punjab announced a Rs10 billion relief package for financial support of 2.5 million families of daily-wage earners.<sup id="cite_ref-punjab_relief_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-punjab_relief-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The country reported an additional 118 cases on 29 March, taking the total to 1,526. One death each was reported in the provinces of Sindh and Khyber Pakhtunkhwa, taking the total number of deceased to 13. Khyber Pakhtunkhwa developed and disseminated quarantine discontinuation guidelines.<sup id="cite_ref-MoNHSRC7_71-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoNHSRC7-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Also on the day, five Pakistani nationals visiting India on medical visas returned home via the <a href="/wiki/Wagah_border" class="mw-redirect" title="Wagah border">Wagah border</a> after being stranded in <a href="/wiki/Noida" title="Noida">Noida</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Delhi" title="New Delhi">New Delhi</a> due to the countrywide 21-day lockdown imposed by the Indian government.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> As the cases neared 500 in Sindh, the CM of the province said that the data showed 25% of cases were due to local transmission. He stated,  "the local transmission ratio is worrisome and needs to be contained further."<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 30 March, the Federal Minister for Science and Technology <a href="/wiki/Chaudhry_Fawad_Hussain" class="mw-redirect" title="Chaudhry Fawad Hussain">Chaudhry Fawad Hussain</a> said that locally manufactured ventilators and testing kits would hit the market in the coming days. The coronavirus testing kits were developed by Pakistan's <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Sciences_and_Technology,_Pakistan" class="mw-redirect" title="National University of Sciences and Technology, Pakistan">National University of Sciences &amp; Technology</a> (NUST) have been handed to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Health_Services,_Regulation_and_Coordination#Drug_Regulatory_Authority_of_Pakistan" title="Ministry of National Health Services, Regulation and Coordination">Drug Regulatory Authority</a> (DRAP) for final approval. While the <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Engineering_Council" title="Pakistan Engineering Council">Pakistan Engineering Council</a> (PEC) developed ventilators, in collaboration with <a href="/wiki/NED_University_of_Engineering_and_Technology" class="mw-redirect" title="NED University of Engineering and Technology">NED University of Engineering and Technology</a> and Pakistan Engineering Board, which were handed over to DRAP later in the week. He also said that the capacity of <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Council_of_Scientific_and_Industrial_Research" title="Pakistan Council of Scientific and Industrial Research">Pakistan Council of Scientific and Industrial Research</a> (PCSIR) for production of hand sanitizers was enhanced.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 31 March, 82 total recoveries were announced, as well as the 26th death in the country. 174 new cases were tested positive, meaning that the total number of positive cases had increased to 2039.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="April_2020">April 2020</span></h3>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_cases">Other cases</span></h2>
<p>On 29 January, four Pakistani students studying in <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> were tested positive for <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">COVID-19</a>. Two more were later confirmed making the total number 6. Four of the students had recovered on 12 February while the other two recovered on 14 February after being hospitalised in <a href="/wiki/Guangzhou" title="Guangzhou">Guangzhou</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 11 March, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Pakistan" title="List of diplomatic missions of Pakistan">Pakistani Consulate</a> in <a href="/wiki/Milan" title="Milan">Milan</a> announced the first death of a Pakistani from COVID-19 in <a href="/wiki/Brescia" title="Brescia">Brescia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A Pakistani national tested positive at the <a href="/wiki/Torkham" title="Torkham">Torkham border</a> between Pakistan and Afghanistan on 12 March. It was reported that the patient was an employee of <a href="/wiki/List_of_diplomatic_missions_of_Pakistan" title="List of diplomatic missions of Pakistan">Pakistani embassy</a> in Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 March, the <a href="/wiki/Health_Minister_of_the_Gaza_Strip" title="Health Minister of the Gaza Strip">Palestinian Health Ministry</a> announced a new case in <a href="/wiki/Salfit_Governorate" title="Salfit Governorate">Salfit Governorate</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a>, which originated from <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> On 21 March, Palestinian sources confirmed the <a href="/wiki/2020_coronavirus_pandemic_in_the_State_of_Palestine" title="2020 coronavirus pandemic in the State of Palestine">first two cases</a> in <a href="/wiki/Gaza_City" title="Gaza City">Gaza City</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gaza_Strip" title="Gaza Strip">Gaza</a>; the two Palestinians had traveled from Pakistan and entered Gaza through <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>. Once they had tested positive for the virus they were placed in quarantine in <a href="/wiki/Rafah" title="Rafah">Rafah</a> since their arrival on 19 March.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 28 March, Pakistani squash player <a href="/wiki/Azam_Khan_(squash_player)" title="Azam Khan (squash player)">Azam Khan</a> died of coronavirus in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Prevention_measures_and_Response">Prevention measures and Response</span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Federal">Federal</span></h3>
<p>The national carrier, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_International_Airlines" title="Pakistan International Airlines">PIA</a> decided to suspend the flight operation between Pakistan and China till January 30 due to the outbreak. After confirmed reports of hundreds of cases in neighbouring <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Civil_Aviation_Authority" title="Pakistan Civil Aviation Authority">Pakistan Civil Aviation Authority</a> (CAA) introduced screening measures at four major airports: <a href="/wiki/Islamabad_International_Airport" title="Islamabad International Airport">Islamabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jinnah_International_Airport" title="Jinnah International Airport">Karachi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Allama_Iqbal_International_Airport" title="Allama Iqbal International Airport">Lahore</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bacha_Khan_International_Airport" title="Bacha Khan International Airport">Peshawar</a> for every passenger arriving from China.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Screening was also started for domestic travellers at Karachi's airport on 21 March.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 13 March, President <a href="/wiki/Arif_Alvi" title="Arif Alvi">Dr. Arif Alvi</a> in a special tweet, advised the public to avoid participation in mass gatherings, handshaking or hugging in addition to taking other precautionary measures if they observe symptoms of flu or coronavirus infection.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> Pakistan also stopped all international flights, except those at <a href="/wiki/Islamabad_International_Airport" title="Islamabad International Airport">Islamabad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jinnah_International_Airport" title="Jinnah International Airport">Karachi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Allama_Iqbal_International_Airport" title="Allama Iqbal International Airport">Lahore</a> airports on the day.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>It was also decided on 13 March at the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Council_(Pakistan)" title="National Security Council (Pakistan)">National Security Council meeting</a> with Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Imran_Khan" title="Imran Khan">Imran Khan</a> that all schools and universities would be closed until 5 April. However, the faculty and staff will go to work as usual. The lectures and classes will be held online in some institutions i.e., Riphah International University, FAST NUCES University, Institute of Space Technology.<sup id="cite_ref-Border_and_school_closures_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Border_and_school_closures-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-school_closures_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-school_closures-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Day" title="Pakistan Day">Pakistan Day Parade</a>, scheduled to be held on 23 March was also cancelled along with all public events<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> and proceedings of the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Pakistan" title="Senate of Pakistan">Senate</a> were postponed for two weeks on the day.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Pakistan closed its borders to travellers from <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Wesh%E2%80%93Chaman_border_crossing" title="Wesh–Chaman border crossing">Chaman border</a> from 2 until 21 March.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The border was only partially reopened later after 21 March for transportation of food items while pedestrian movement remained suspended.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>  The <a href="/wiki/Durand_Line" title="Durand Line">Durand Line border</a> was sealed from 16 March for at least two weeks. The same time period also applied to <a href="/wiki/Taftan,_Balochistan" title="Taftan, Balochistan">the land border with Iran</a> after reopening it on 7 March from a previous closure.<sup id="cite_ref-Border_and_school_closures_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Border_and_school_closures-93">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> All land borders, including the <a href="/wiki/China%E2%80%93Pakistan_border" title="China–Pakistan border">China-Pakistan border</a> with <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> were shut from 16 March.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Lieutenant General Muhammad Afzal, the <a href="/wiki/National_Disaster_Management_Authority_(Pakistan)" title="National Disaster Management Authority (Pakistan)">NDMA</a> chairman, announced that the government was working on securing more PPEs and other resources for healthcare workers on 20 March.<sup id="cite_ref-doctors_complain_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doctors_complain-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 21 March, all international flights were suspended for two weeks. The Civil Aviation Authority stated, “[The] government of Pakistan has decided to suspend operation of all international passenger, chartered and private flights to Pakistan, effective from March 21 till April 4”.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> This led to many citizens being stranded in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> The Railways Minister <a href="/wiki/Sheikh_Rasheed_Ahmed" class="mw-redirect" title="Sheikh Rasheed Ahmed">Sheikh Rasheed Ahmed</a> declared the suspension of 42 trains.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_National_Health_Services,_Regulation_and_Coordination" title="Ministry of National Health Services, Regulation and Coordination">health ministry</a> announced that 14 metric tonnes of PPE, "including face masks, thermometers, gloves [and] gowns", had been dispatched to Pakistan on 22 March.<sup id="cite_ref-doctors_complain_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doctors_complain-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> The federal government offered financial assistance to Sindh by allotting the province $10 million from the non-development funds of the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> the same day. <a href="/wiki/Imran_Ismail" title="Imran Ismail">Imran Ismail</a>, the Governor of Sindh stated that the federal government was taking "vigorous measures" to control the outbreak and that rations will be provided to the families of patients.<sup id="cite_ref-Sindh_response_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sindh_response-107">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 March, the nation celebrated <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Day" title="Pakistan Day">Pakistan Day</a> without any public gatherings or military parade. The Prime Minister Imran Khan and President Dr. Arif Alvi urged the nation to demonstrate unity, discipline and passion in fighting the coronavirus pandemic.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> The PM also stated that a complete lockdown of the country was not feasible as 25% of the population lives below the poverty line and would make their lives miserable.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> The government has over 35 hospitals across the country set up to deal with the outbreak, equipped with more than 118,000 beds as of the day.<sup id="cite_ref-doctors_complain_59-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-doctors_complain-59">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Pakistan" title="National Assembly of Pakistan">National Assembly</a> speaker <a href="/wiki/Asad_Qaiser" title="Asad Qaiser">Asad Qaiser</a> summoned a meeting of the parliamentary leaders of the Senate and the <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_Pakistan" title="National Assembly of Pakistan">Lower house</a> to review and discuss the role of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Pakistan" title="Parliament of Pakistan">Parliament</a> in containing the spread of the pandemic across the country for 25 March on the day.<sup id="cite_ref-NA_meeting_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NA_meeting-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 March, the Chief of the Army Staff General <a href="/wiki/Qamar_Javed_Bajwa" title="Qamar Javed Bajwa">Qamar Javed Bajwa</a> ordered the deployment of troops nationwide and military's medical resources to fight the ongoing outbreak alongside the national health infrastructure after the Ministry of Interior approved the action on the previous day. The Ministry had received requests in this regard from the provincial governments over the past two days amid surging number of patients.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/State_Bank_of_Pakistan" title="State Bank of Pakistan">State Bank of Pakistan</a> issued a statement the same day declaring that it would be providing disinfected cash to all banks for circulation while ensuring to "clean, disinfect, seal and quarantine all cash being collected from hospitals and clinics and to block circulation of such cash in the market." It was further assured that banks could re-issue cash which remained in quarantine for 15 days and all ATMs as well as call centres and helplines would be running 24/7. Banks could close branches only if a staff member tested positive for the virus or "where requisite human resources [were] not available” to avoid congestion as it would be counterproductive to <a href="/wiki/Social_distancing" title="Social distancing">social distancing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 26 March, Pakistan decided to seek $3.7 billion additional financing from three multilateral creditors including another loan of $1.4 billion from the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> to cope with the challenges being posed by the novel coronavirus outbreak. Adviser to the PM on Finance Dr <a href="/wiki/Abdul_Hafeez_Shaikh" title="Abdul Hafeez Shaikh">Abdul Hafeez Shaikh</a> announced at a news conference that the <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">World Bank</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Asian_Development_Bank" title="Asian Development Bank">Asian Development Bank</a> would also extend loans of $1 billion and $1.25 billion respectively to the country.
</p><p>The PM announced formation of youth force labelled ‘Corona Relief Tigers’ to help government in fight against the spread of coronavirus nationwide on 27 March. The force was distributed across the country and would be used to supply food items to people in their houses in case Covid-19 cases sharply rose in a locality. The recruitment began on 31 March.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to various lockdowns imposed by the regional governments, the goods transport system came to a halt in later March. Thus, the federal government decided on 29 March that highways and roads across the country would remain open to ensure the transportation of goods and also increased the number of freight trains to avert a shortage of food and other essential supplies. Chairing a meeting, the Prime Minister asked the provincial governments to take strict action against hoarders and profiteers who were trying to exploit the ongoing crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-martyrs_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-martyrs-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> By late March, many regions in Pakistan had considered releasing under-trial prisoners to curb the outbreak in jails. However, on 30 March, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Pakistan" title="Supreme Court of Pakistan">Supreme Court</a> refrained high courts and federal and provincial governments to pass any order regarding the release of under-trial prisoners.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_Relief_Package">Economic Relief Package</span></h4>
<p>On 24 March, the Prime Minister approved a Rs1.2 trillion economic relief package. Of this, a total of Rs150 billion was allotted for low-income groups, particularly laborers while 280 billion rupees ($1.76 billion) was assigned for wheat procurement. Loan interest payments for exporters were deferred temporarily, while a package of 100 billion rupees ($63 million) was provided to support small industries and the agriculture sector. There was also a significant deduction in petroleum prices and the public couple pay electricity and gas bills below a certain amount in installments.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> Under the package the monthly stipend of the <a href="/wiki/Benazir_Income_Support_Programme" title="Benazir Income Support Programme">Benazir Income Support Programme</a> (BISP) was increased from Rs2,000 to Rs3,000. It was decided that the funds of the government's Ehsaas programme would be distributed among the poor according to the available data of the BISP and through the under progress National Socio-Economic Registry (NSER) of the BISP. The total number of BISP beneficiaries was 5.2 million but the number was increased under the package.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The relief package also included a special package for healthcare professionals. According to which, if a doctor or a paramedic died while treating coronavirus patients, they would be considered martyrs and their families would receive the package that is given to martyrs.<sup id="cite_ref-martyrs_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-martyrs-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The federal cabinet reviewed and approved the economic relief package on 31 March. The <a href="/wiki/Economic_Coordination_Committee_(Pakistan)" title="Economic Coordination Committee (Pakistan)">Economic Coordination Committee</a> (ECC) finalised the package, including a Rs100-billion supplementary grant for an Emergency Relief Fund to combat the pandemic. It also approved a special package for relief to 12 million poor families through cash assistance under the Ehsaas Programme, where cash grants would be provided under the Kafalat Programme and emergency cash assistance to the poor on the recommendation of the district administration. The financial assistance was provided for four months as a one-time dispensation. The cash would be provided either in one Rs12,000 installment through Kafalat partner banks, <a href="/wiki/Bank_Alfalah" title="Bank Alfalah">Bank Alfalah</a> and <a href="/wiki/Habib_Bank_Limited" title="Habib Bank Limited">Habib Bank Limited</a> after biometric verification or in two installments of Rs6,000 each.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
