<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Punjab">Punjab</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Punjab,_Pakistan" title="Government of Punjab, Pakistan">Government</a> of Punjab declared a health emergency on 12 March in a cabinet meeting. A quarantine facility was established in the <a href="/wiki/Dera_Ghazi_Khan" title="Dera Ghazi Khan">Dera Ghazi Khan</a> district for the pilgrims returning from <a href="/wiki/2020_coronavirus_pandemic_in_Iran" title="2020 coronavirus pandemic in Iran">Iran</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-school_closures_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-school_closures-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 22 March, the government decided to close down shopping malls, markets, parks and public gathering places for two days till 24 March. Punjab Chief Minister, <a href="/wiki/Sardar_Usman_Buzdar" title="Sardar Usman Buzdar">Sardar Usman Buzdar</a> urged people to stay at home, practice <a href="/wiki/Social_distancing" title="Social distancing">social distancing</a> and avoid unnecessary travel.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, local media reported that many residents in Lahore had failed to practice the measures and downright defied it by opening up businesses and gathering in large numbers on various public grounds. This led to the local police and city administration to forcibly vacate them.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 March, The Chief Minister announced a 14 days lockdown from 24 March till 6 April. All markets, shopping malls and public places were closed and <a href="/wiki/Pillion" title="Pillion">pillion</a> riding was banned.<sup id="cite_ref-punjab_lockdown_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-punjab_lockdown-4">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> He also announced that a 1,000 bed hospital would be setup in <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">Lahore</a> while five other hospitals were designated for coronavirus patients across the province the next day on 23 March while the local government and rescue services started disinfecting towns and cities. Public bus services were also temporarily suspended to disinfect all buses and stations.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> The Secretary Home Department of Punjab wrote a letter one the day to the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Interior_(Pakistan)" title="Ministry of Interior (Pakistan)">Ministry of Interior</a> seeking the assistance of the military under Article 245.<sup id="cite_ref-NA_meeting_110-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NA_meeting-110">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Punjab" title="University of the Punjab">Punjab University</a> manufactured coronavirus protection kits along with large amounts of hand sanitisers, disinfectants and antiseptic wet-tissues for the public. The sanitisers are for national usage. An online initiative was started for online purchases for home deliveries.<sup id="cite_ref-university_action_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-university_action-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> Also on the day, more than 150 pilgrims arrived in <a href="/wiki/Faisalabad" title="Faisalabad">Faisalabad</a> from Iran via the Taftan border to be quarantined at a centre. More arrangements were made to quarantine another 450 pilgrims returning at a centre established in the campus of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Agriculture,_Faisalabad" title="University of Agriculture, Faisalabad">Agricultural University</a>. The government established the largest quarantine centre in the nation in <a href="/wiki/Multan" title="Multan">Multan</a> at Multan Industrial Estate to isolate the returning pilgrims with 3000 rooms. It had 1,247 pilgrims in quarantine as of the day. A companion 50 bed hospital was also setup to aid the centre.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The NIH initiated district level training of <a href="/wiki/High-dependency_unit" title="High-dependency unit">high-dependency unit</a>, isolation and quarantine staff across the province on 27 March.<sup id="cite_ref-MoNHSRC7_71-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoNHSRC7-71">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Chief Minister of the province announced a Rs10 billion relief package for financial support of 2.5 million families of daily-wage earners on 28 March. Each family was entitled to Rs4,000 financial assistance excluding the beneficiaries of the Benazir Income Support Programme (BISP).<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> The government also decided to remove provincial taxes to the tune of Rs18bn. The CM said that  the Punjab government had decided to use its special powers for granting 90-day imprisonment rebate to prisoners in jails across the province which would benefit some 3,100 prisoners. Furthermore, the Punjab Infectious Diseases Prevention and Control Ordinance, 2020, was implemented to allow the civil administration and health department to implement government measures with complete ease and under the cover of law. It was also declared that the government would provide a month's additional salary to all healthcare workers across Punjab.<sup id="cite_ref-punjab_relief_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-punjab_relief-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> The Punjab Minister for Finance Hashim Jawan Bakht said that the economic package would also help the health sector and the Provincial Disaster Management Authority (PDMA) cope with the crisis with an immediate funding of Rs11.5 billion. To aid the medical professionals, a textile owner from Lahore offered to manufacture PPE voluntarily and free of cost.<sup id="cite_ref-punjab_relief2_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-punjab_relief2-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Also in the meeting, the CM stated that laboratories around the province would test 3,200 people every day for coronavirus and 10,000 doctors and paramedics were being recruited to fight the pandemic.<sup id="cite_ref-martyrs_115-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-martyrs-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sindh">Sindh</span></h4>
<h5><span class="mw-headline" id="March">March</span></h5>
<p>On 1 March, <a href="/wiki/Chief_Minister_of_Sindh" title="Chief Minister of Sindh">Chief Minister of Sindh</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syed_Murad_Ali_Shah" title="Syed Murad Ali Shah">Syed Murad Ali Shah</a>, announced the closure of all educational institutes in Sindh until 13 March,<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> which was later extended until 30 May.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> On 12 March, <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Sindh" title="Government of Sindh">the Government of Sindh</a> also announced that the remaining <a href="/wiki/2020_Pakistan_Super_League" title="2020 Pakistan Super League">PSL matches</a> at <a href="/wiki/National_Stadium,_Karachi" title="National Stadium, Karachi">National Stadium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a> would be held <a href="/wiki/Behind_closed_doors_(sport)" title="Behind closed doors (sport)">behind closed doors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> The Sindh government announced on 13 March that all educational institutions will remain closed until 30 May<sup id="cite_ref-school_closures_94-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-school_closures-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> imposed a temporary ban on marriage halls, shrines and festivals in the province on 14 March.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 20 March, the <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Army" title="Pakistan Army">Pakistan Army</a> helped setup a 10,000-bed field hospital at Karachi's <a href="/wiki/Expo_Centre" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Expo Centre">Expo Centre</a> to isolate and treat confirmed patients. ALl expenses for its establishment were born by the provincial government.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> On 21 March, the Government of Sindh announced a lockdown in the province for 14 days from morning of 24 March, ordering all public transport, markets, offices, shopping malls, restaurants, and public areas to be shut down.<sup id="cite_ref-sindh_lockdown_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sindh_lockdown-5">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-lockdowns_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lockdowns-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> The Sindh government announced paid leave for all workers during the lockdown, and said no would be laid off during the period under Section 3 of the Sindh Epidemic Diseases Act (2014) and other relevant labor laws.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> The province banned intra-city transport to minimize the outbreak and multiple violators were issued fines, impounded and canceled.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup>
The <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_army" class="mw-redirect" title="Pakistan army">national army</a> was called to enfore the lockdown.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> On 23 March, an isolation and quarantine centre was completed at the <a href="/wiki/Jinnah_Postgraduate_Medical_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Jinnah Postgraduate Medical College">Jinnah Postgraduate Medical College</a> in Karachi which also provided free tests of suspected cases with results in 8 hours of sample submission.<sup id="cite_ref-university_action_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-university_action-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Cricket_Board" title="Pakistan Cricket Board">Pakistan Cricket Board</a>, on request from the Sindh Government, agreed to convert its Hanif Mohammad High Performance Centre into a temporary living area for paramedic staff working at the makeshift hospital at Expo Centre, Karachi on 24 March.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> The local police detained 472 people in various districts of the province on the day, with 222 of them in Karachi alone and a total of <a href="/wiki/First_information_report" title="First information report">FIRs</a> were registered. The cases pertained to hoarding and profiteering of safety masks and hand sanitisers, large gatherings, opening shops and restaurants and travelling in passenger buses. Multiple violations of the lockdown were observed in several places across the province such as gatherings on the beach, residents being out and major markets, shopping centres, <a href="/wiki/Bazaar" title="Bazaar">bazaars</a> and restaurants remained open.<sup id="cite_ref-lockdown_arrests_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lockdown_arrests-64">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> As a result, a taskforce meeting led by the Chief Minister was held on the next day on 25 March to take more stringent measures to ensure that all residents abided by the government orders of. It was resolved that all grocery stores and shops apart from pharmacies and medical stores to remain closed between 8pm and 8am. The Sindh Inspector General of Police, Javed Ahmed Mahar was directed to make measures taken in connection with the lockdown and make certain that people were not allowed to roam freely in the city unnecessarily. Additionally, the Chief Secretary and Karachi Commissioner were ordered to ensure that big factories remained closed during the lockdown and direct banks to keep only important branches operational.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 March, the provincial health department officials began coronavirus case mapping as per directives by the Chief Minister. He further tasked them with sharing the data with deputy commissioners so necessary measures could be taken to contain the outbreak in their respective areas. Orders were also given to improve sampling arrangements, upon which 18 vehicles of the Indus Hospital were dedicated for collecting samples from homes. The health officials briefed the Chief Minister about a new machine made at at the <a href="/wiki/Wuhan_Institute_of_Virology" title="Wuhan Institute of Virology">Wuhan Institute of Virology</a> in China, which could test secretions from the nose instead of testing throat secretion as was the current procedure.
At this, the CM directed the provincial Chief Secretary to consult with medical experts whether procuring the machine would be feasible and if they deemed it to be beneficial, place an order for 100 machines. The CM further stated that he would request the federal government for a special aircraft to transport the machines if the government decided to procure them.<sup id="cite_ref-pilgrims_return_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pilgrims_return-65">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On the same day, the local government also arranged to launch a mobile service across the province to provide rations to the needy along with daily wagers to those affected by the pandemic. A number was dedicated for the service and those in need could text there. Moreover, a warehouse was established for storage of ration bags and a helpline set up for people to register for acquiring the bags. The CM also ordered to release Rs341 million for carrying out administrative work under district administrations and spending on facilities provided to pilgrims.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> However, reports emerged that rations were being denied to the <a href="/wiki/Hinduism_in_Pakistan" title="Hinduism in Pakistan">minority Hindus</a>. They were told that the supplies were only meant for Muslims.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 March, public holidays were extended till 5 April in the province while markets and shopping malls were to remain closed till 10 April. Ajmal Wazir, the adviser to the CM stated that the government the government had decided on tax exemption to facilitate the business community and protect jobs with Rs17.5 billion reserved for wheat procurement. An amount of Rs8 billion was also approved for district hospitals to enable them by the urgent supplies.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> To further enforce lockdown, the Sindh govt restricted movement between 8AM and 5PM, while all grocery stores were ordered to be closed by 5 PM. These restrictions went into force on 28 March.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Sindh Province also received 500,000 K <a href="/wiki/N95_mask" title="N95 mask">N95 masks</a> from <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MoNHSRC3_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoNHSRC3-146">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> On 29 March, the Sindh CM approved a proposal to release about 4,000 convicts from prison in order to prevent the spread of the novel coronavirus outbreak in the province's jails.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 30 March, the Chief Minister, Syed Murad Ali Shah made public a mobile application, namely the Sindh Relief Initiative, on which welfare organisations could register to work with the provincial government for the distribution of ration among daily-wagers at their doorstep.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Also on the day, the Mayor of Karachi, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Wasim_Akhtar&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Wasim Akhtar (page does not exist)">Wasim Akhtar</a> designated five cemeteries in the city for burials of those who died due to coronavirus. He said that only a few close relatives of the deceased could enter the cemetery for burial, adding that the body would be brought into the cemetery with protective measures and no last sighting would be allowed. The mayor also wrote to the National Disaster Management Authority, the provincial government and the Governor <a href="/wiki/Imran_Ismail" title="Imran Ismail">Imran Ismail</a> requesting funds to provide essential equipment and ventilators to Karachi Metropolitan Corporation hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> The Sindh government issued a circular directing private schools across the province to pay full salaries to its teachers on time the same day. Another directive was also declared for factories and other private entities operating in the province to disburse salaries to their employees by 31 March.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Balochistan">Balochistan</span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Balochistan,_Pakistan" title="Government of Balochistan, Pakistan">Balochistan Government</a> constituted a 14-member technical committee in late January to tackle the outbreak.<sup id="cite_ref-early_measures_151-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-early_measures-151">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> All schools have been closed till 31 March. Balochistan Minister Sardar Yar Mohammad Rind stated that "action will be taken against schools that do not comply with the decision". Matric exams have also been postponed.<sup id="cite_ref-school_closures_94-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-school_closures-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The province like others also requested for the army to be deployed.<sup id="cite_ref-lockdowns_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-lockdowns-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 March, the Balochistan government imposed a complete lockdown in the entire province until 7 Aril. It included a complete ban on public getting out of their homes, all kinds of social and religious gatherings or any public or private event. All public and private offices were ordered closed. Exemptions included essential services such as personnel of hospitals, laboratories and medical stores, law enforcement agencies, people in need of urgent medical care with one attendant, one person per family going out to buy grocery and medicines within the vicinity of their residence and burials of people that had passed away. Only one person was allowed to travel in a private vehicle. Media personnel authorized by concerned media houses and newspaper hawkers were allowed to move freely as well. Public and private telecom companies, essential staff of banks with limited public dealing, defence-related manufacturing industries, food items manufacturing industries and distribution offices, grocery shops, petrol pumps and auto workshops and welfare organizations providing services were given permission to operate. Similar to Gilgit-Baltistan and Islamad, Section 144 was also enforced.<sup id="cite_ref-balochistan_lockdown_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-balochistan_lockdown-6">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> A state of emergency was imposed in five districts which bordered Iran on 24 March.<sup id="cite_ref-islamabad_measures_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-islamabad_measures-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Khyber_Pakhtunkhwa">Khyber Pakhtunkhwa</span></h4>
<p>The provincial <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Khyber_Pakhtunkhwa" title="Government of Khyber Pakhtunkhwa">Government</a> has closed all educational institutes until 5 April and postponed all public gatherings until further notice as a preventive measure.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-school_closures_94-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-school_closures-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> All inter-district public transport was banned for seven days on 22 March.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 24 March, the <a href="/wiki/Peshawar_High_Court" title="Peshawar High Court">Peshawar High Court</a> decided to shut down all courts in the province until March 28. Only essential staff were allowed to come to courts with no more than one official in the office.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> On 27 March, screening teams were deputed at all district entry and exit points for screening of visitors of Covid-19 patients.<sup id="cite_ref-MoNHSRC5_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoNHSRC5-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Chief Minister of the province <a href="/wiki/Mahmood_Khan" title="Mahmood Khan">Mahmood Khan</a> announced on 26 March that the government had appointed at least 1,300 new doctors on contractual basis across the province to help stem the spread of coronavirus. The KP Public Service Commission also approved the recruitment of 635 more doctors to join the province's health force.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 29 March, the government approved a Rs32 billion stimulus economic package to provide relief to the masses and the business community amid the coronavirus crisis.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> Provincial Information Minister Ajmal Wazir, announced at a press conference that the relief package include Rs11.4 billion benefiting 1.9 million deserving families, Rs3,000 would be given under the Ehsaas programme and Rs2,000 by the KP government. He added that the business community had also been exempted from taxes worth Rs5 billion and the provincial government had ramped up its testing capacity with 500 new diagnostics kits.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gilgit-Baltistan">Gilgit-Baltistan</span></h4>
<p>On 12 March, the region's <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Gilgit-Baltistan" title="Government of Gilgit-Baltistan">Government</a> declared medical emergency in the province after more cases of were reported. Educational institutes were further closed until 5 April as a preventive measure.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-school_closures_94-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-school_closures-94">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> Similar to Islamabad, Section 144 was also imposed on 21 March.<sup id="cite_ref-section_144_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-section_144-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The provincial government decided to put the entire region on lockdown for an indefinite period on 22 March and suspended intercity transport services. Para-military forces were also tasked to ensure the lockdown.<sup id="cite_ref-gb_lockdown_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gb_lockdown-8">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 27 March, the Chinese government handed medical equipments and 10 tonnes of other goods to the Gilgit-Baltistan government to help it fight Covid-19. The equipment included five ventilators, 2,000 N95 masks, 200,000 face masks, 2,000 testing kits and medical protective kits.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> The same day, the government decided that all suspected travelers coming from the Taftan border would be tested for Covid-19.<sup id="cite_ref-MoNHSRC5_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MoNHSRC5-70">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Azad_Kashmir">Azad Kashmir</span></h4>
<p>On 14 March, the local <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Azad_Kashmir" title="Government of Azad Kashmir">Government</a> declared a health emergency after a meeting of the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Council_(Pakistan)" title="National Security Council (Pakistan)">National Security Council</a>. It also announced closure of educational institutions until 6 April and secondary examinations were postponed. AJK Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Raja_Farooq_Haider" class="mw-redirect" title="Raja Farooq Haider">Raja Farooq Haider</a> also stated that screening mechanisms were installed at all 11 points of entry while quarantine facilities were being established in all 10 districts.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> On 21 March, a suspension of all inter-provincial transport for three days was imposed. No public transport vehicles were allowed to either enter or leave the province. It warned that violators would be punished under the Epidemic Diseases Act.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 23 March, The AJK Prime Minister announced a 3-week lockdown for the region. Movement was restricted and special passes were issued for journalists and people travelling under inevitable circumstances while only one person from each family was allowed to go out to get food essentials.<sup id="cite_ref-ajk_lockdown_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ajk_lockdown-7">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Islamabad">Islamabad</span></h4>
<p>On 21 March, the city administration imposed Section 144 on the region for 15 days. All restaurants and shopping malls were ordered to be closed and violators could face legal consequences.<sup id="cite_ref-section_144_160-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-section_144-160">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> The local Union Council in the Bhara Kahu region was sealed after 11 suspected cases emerged from there on 23 March.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 25 March, the national government shut the outpatient departments of hospitals in the capital territory to stem the spread of the virus, only the emergency services remained optional. The capital's Deputy Commissioner, Hamza Shafqat issued a notification declaring 'a complete ban on intra-city, inter-district and inter-province movement of people by public transport. However, the metro bus service will be functional but at a distance of one seat between passengers.' Furthermore, gatherings of all kinds at public and private places were banned no one was allowed to move out of their respective union councils.<sup id="cite_ref-islamabad_measures_66-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-islamabad_measures-66">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Impact">Impact</span></h2>
<table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2020_coronavirus_pandemic_in_Pakistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2020</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span></h3>
<p>On 22 March, Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Imran_Khan" title="Imran Khan">Imran Khan</a> urged the United States President <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a> to temporarily lift sanctions on Iran. He stated on Twitter, 'I want to appeal to President Trump on humanitarian grounds to lift the <a href="/wiki/Sanctions_against_Iran" title="Sanctions against Iran">sanctions</a> against Iran till the COVID-19 pandemic is over.'<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The same day, the Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Shah_Mehmood_Qureshi" class="mw-redirect" title="Shah Mehmood Qureshi">Shah Mehmood Qureshi</a> raised the issue of external debt faced by the country and how it should be relieved in repayment of loans on the phone with <a href="/wiki/Heiko_Maas" title="Heiko Maas">Heiko Maas</a>, the German Foreign Minister. Qureshi reportedly told Maas that united efforts were required for dealing with the pandemic and that debt relief could help Pakistan in better handling of the outbreak in the country. He further stated that sanctions on <a href="/wiki/Iran" title="Iran">Iran</a> should be lifted immediately so it could utilise its own resources to fight the ongoing outbreak there. In response, Maas assured him that the issues would be raised at the forthcoming <a href="/wiki/G7" class="mw-redirect" title="G7">G7</a> meeting and the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> Foreign Ministers’ Conference next week.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> He also echoed the need to lift sanctions on Iran on calls with the French Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Jean-Yves_Le_Drian" title="Jean-Yves Le Drian">Jean-Yves Le Drian</a><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> and the Spanish Foreign Minister <a href="/wiki/Arancha_Gonzalez" class="mw-redirect" title="Arancha Gonzalez">Arancha Gonzalez</a><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> on 24 March.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h3>
<table class="box-Expand_section plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" decoding="async" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2020_coronavirus_pandemic_in_Pakistan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2020</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare_professionals">Healthcare professionals</span></h3>
<p>The federal government's economic relief package also benefited the healthcare professionals in the country. It was decided that if a doctor or a paramedic died while treating coronavirus patients, they would be considered martyrs and their families would receive the package that is given to martyrs.<sup id="cite_ref-martyrs_115-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-martyrs-115">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Making a landmark, the Pakistani <a href="/wiki/Police_in_Pakistan" class="mw-redirect" title="Police in Pakistan">Law enforcement</a>  presented the <a href="/wiki/Guard_of_honour#Pakistan" title="Guard of honour">Guard of honour</a> as a mark of respect from 27–29 March to the doctors and para medical staff fighting on the front lines of the global COVID-19 outbreak across the nation in Sukkur,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Quetta,<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> and Dera Islamil Khan.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> The medical staff of a Mayo hospital in Lahore were given a guard of honor by the Lahore police for their efforts to help Pakistan fight the coronavirus pandemic.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup>  Observing social distance (home-quarantined) citizens of Pakistan together with celebrities raised white flags on 27 March across Pakistan from their balconies, rooftops expressing love for the doctors and para-medics who are combating without fearing from the epidemic COVID-19 virus.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Government of Punjab announced a one-month honorarium for the healthcare workers at the end of March. This meant that in case a healthcare worker lost their life, a martyr package was included in the regional government's relief package. Medical professionals across the province were also provided with one-month additional salary in recognition of their services.<sup id="cite_ref-punjab_relief_74-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-punjab_relief-74">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-punjab_relief2_129-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-punjab_relief2-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Impact_of_the_2019%E2%80%9320_coronavirus_pandemic_on_sports#Cricket" title="Impact of the 2019–20 coronavirus pandemic on sports">Impact of the 2019–20 coronavirus pandemic on sports §&#160;Cricket</a></div>
<p>Fears of the <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">coronavirus disease</a> spreading alarmed the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Sindh" title="Government of Sindh">Sindh provincial government</a>, who announced on 13 March that remaining matches of the <a href="/wiki/2020_Pakistan_Super_League" title="2020 Pakistan Super League">2020 Pakistan Super League (PSL)</a>, scheduled in <a href="/wiki/Karachi" title="Karachi">Karachi</a>, would be played <a href="/wiki/Behind_closed_doors_(sport)" title="Behind closed doors (sport)">behind closed doors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Cricket_Board" title="Pakistan Cricket Board">Pakistan Cricket Board (PCB)</a> offered international players participating in PSL to leave for their home countries (if they wish so), while PSL continues as per schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> 10 international players and one international staff member opted to leave the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/2020_Pakistan_Super_League_Final" class="mw-redirect" title="2020 Pakistan Super League Final">Final match</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lahore" title="Lahore">Lahore</a>, was rescheduled to 18 March instead of 22 March.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 17 March 2020, the knockout fixtures (both Semi Finals and Final) of Pakistan Super League (PSL) were indefinitely postponed due to the sudden spike in coronavirus cases in Pakistan.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After six years, when <a href="/wiki/Football_Federation_League" title="Football Federation League">Pakistan Football Federation League</a> returned, the matches were played before 16 March 2020. On 16 March 2020, the <a href="/wiki/Pakistan_Football_Federation" title="Pakistan Football Federation">Pakistan Football Federation</a> released a notification announcing that the matches were postponed.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Impact_of_the_2019%E2%80%9320_coronavirus_pandemic_on_religion" title="Impact of the 2019–20 coronavirus pandemic on religion">Impact of the 2019–20 coronavirus pandemic on religion</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Coutts" title="Joseph Coutts">Cardinal Joseph Coutts</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> implored the faithful to follow proper measures to prevent the spread of the coronavirus and encouraged interfaith solidarity amidst the pandemic:<sup id="cite_ref-Hussain2020_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hussain2020-182">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886047036">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>I also call upon my Christian brethren who would want to come to churches on Friday and Sunday to avoid large gatherings. In the end, the Almighty will reward you for your intentions. If we can’t go to a church, mosque or temple, we can pray or worship at home with our families, God shall hear us. We, the people of all faiths, should pray to God to save us from this plague.<sup id="cite_ref-Hussain2020_182-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hussain2020-182">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-tn-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-tn_3-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This number is as reported by daily situation report published by the National Institute of Health at the beginning of the day. It reflects the total cases registered by the authority on previous day and hence does not constitute the current day's cases. It is needed here as the top official source of the country and also the cases reported by the tracker have differed compared to it before.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-121"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-121">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">As of 23 March 2020.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-183"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-183">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The report is released at the start of the day and shows the confirmed cases, recoveries and deaths of the previous day. It is currently the most reliable and top source for the pandemic in the country. Any live trackers either of the govt and of various news media outlets have discrepancies in them and are not as efficient as the report making it redundant to edit the table according to them.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
